assets
 management considers whether it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will not be
realized. The ultimate realization of deferred tax assets is dependent upon future generation for taxable income during the periods
in which temporary differences representing net future deductible amounts become deductible. Management considers the scheduled
reversal of deferred tax liabilities
 projected future taxable income and tax planning strategies in making this assessment. After
consideration of all the information available
 Management believes that significant uncertainty exists with respect to future
realization of the deferred tax assets and has therefore established a full valuation allowance. For the years ended January 31
2017 and 2016
 the change in the valuation allowance was $211
139 and $1
405
640.


&rsquo;s financial
statements. ASC 740 prescribes a comprehensive model for how a company should recognize
 present
 and disclose uncertain positions
that the Company has taken or expects to take in its tax return. For those benefits to be recognized
 a tax position must be more-likely-than-not
to be sustained upon examination by taxing authorities. Differences between tax positions taken or expected to be taken in a tax
return and the net benefit recognized and measured pursuant to the interpretation are referred to as &ldquo;unrecognized benefits.&rdquo;
A liability is recognized (or amount of net operating loss carry forward or amount of tax refundable is reduced) for unrecognized
tax benefit because it represents an enterprise&rsquo;s potential future obligation to the taxing authority for a tax position
that was not recognized as a result of applying the provisions of ASC 740.


 interest costs related to the
unrecognized tax benefits are required to be calculated and would be classified as &ldquo;Other expenses &ndash; Interest&rdquo;
in the statement of operations. Penalties would be recognized as a component of &ldquo;General and administrative.&rdquo;


recorded during the years ended January 31
 2017 and 2016
 respectively. As of January 31
 2017 and 2016
 no liability for unrecognized
tax benefits was required to be reported. The Company does not expect any significant changes in its unrecognized tax benefits
in the next year.

with the requirements of Section 13(a) or 15(d) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 1 - Nature of Operations and Basis&#13;of Presentation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Nature of Operations&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;MamaMancini&amp;#8217;s Holdings, Inc. (the &amp;#8220;Company&amp;#8221;),&#13;(formerly known as Mascot Properties, Inc.) was organized on July 22, 2009 as a Nevada corporation. The Company has a year-end&#13;of January 31.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company is a manufacturer and distributor&#13;of beef meatballs with sauce, turkey meatballs with sauce, beef meat loaf and other similar meats and sauces. The Company&amp;#8217;s&#13;customers are located throughout the United States, with a large concentration in the Northeast and Southeast.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Basis of Presentation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The consolidated financial statements and related&#13;notes have been prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America (&amp;#8220;US&#13;GAAP&amp;#8221;) and include the accounts of the Company and its wholly-owned subsidiaries. All material intercompany balances and&#13;transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company adopted Accounting Standards Update&#13;(&amp;#8220;ASU&amp;#8221;) 2015-03, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Interest-Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30): Simplifying the Presentation of Debt&#13;Issuance Costs,&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt; during the first quarter of 2016. In accordance with the guidance, $26,620 of unamortized debt issuance&#13;costs, associated with the Company&amp;#8217;s debt, were reclassified from other assets, as previously reported on the Consolidated&#13;Balance Sheet as of January 31, 2016, to line of credit, net.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #252525&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #252525&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Going Concern Analysis&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #252525&gt;&lt;i&gt;Going Concern Analysis&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; color: #252525&gt;The Company had a net loss&#13;of $289,140 and $3,511,618 for the years ended January 31, 2017 and 2016. As a result, these conditions had raised substantial&#13;doubt regarding our ability to continue as a going concern. However, as of January 31, 2017, we had cash and working capital of&#13;$666,580 and $1,753,671, respectively. During the year ended January 31, 2017, the Company generated cash from operations of $482,792.&#13;In addition, management was able to negotiate the terms of its note payable with one of the lenders and intends to exercise an&#13;option to extend the maturity date of the note payable to May 1, 2018. Also, the continued revenue growth coupled with improved&#13;gross margins and control of expenses leads management to conclude that it is probable that the Company&amp;#8217;s cash resources&#13;will be sufficient to meet our cash requirements through the first quarter of fiscal year ended January 31, 2019. If necessary,&#13;management also determined that it is probable that external sources of debt and/or equity financing could be obtained based on&#13;management&amp;#8217;s history of being able to raise capital coupled with current favorable market conditions. As a result of both&#13;management&amp;#8217;s plans and current favorable trends in improving cash flow, the Company concluded that the initial conditions&#13;which raised substantial doubt regarding the ability to continue as a going concern have been alleviated. Therefore, the accompanying&#13;consolidated financial statements have been prepared assuming that the Company will continue as a going concern.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 17.4pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 2 - Summary of Significant&#13;Accounting Policies&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Use of Estimates&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The preparation of consolidated financial&#13;statements in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions&#13;that affect the amounts reported in the consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Such estimates and assumptions&#13;impact, among others, the following: allowance for doubtful accounts, inventory obsolescence and the fair value of share-based&#13;payments.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Making estimates requires management&#13;to exercise significant judgment. It is at least reasonably possible that the estimate of the effect of a condition, situation&#13;or set of circumstances that existed at the date of the consolidated financial statements, which management considered in formulating&#13;its estimate could change in the near term due to one or more future confirming events. Accordingly, the actual results could differ&#13;significantly from our estimates.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Risks and Uncertainties&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company operates in an industry&#13;that is subject to intense competition and change in consumer demand. The Company&amp;#8217;s operations are subject to significant&#13;risk and uncertainties including financial and operational risks including the potential risk of business failure.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has experienced, and in&#13;the future expects to continue to experience, variability in sales and earnings. The factors expected to contribute to this variability&#13;include, among others, (i) the cyclical nature of the grocery industry, (ii) general economic conditions in the various local markets&#13;in which the Company competes, including a potential general downturn in the economy, and (iii) the volatility of prices pertaining&#13;to food and beverages in connection with the Company&amp;#8217;s distribution of the product. These factors, among others, make it&#13;difficult to project the Company&amp;#8217;s operating results on a consistent basis.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cash&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company considers all highly liquid&#13;instruments purchased with a maturity of three months or less to be cash equivalents. The Company held no cash equivalents at January&#13;31, 2017 or January 31, 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company minimizes its credit risk&#13;associated with cash by periodically evaluating the credit quality of its primary financial institution. The balance at times may&#13;exceed federally insured limits.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Accounts Receivable and Allowance&#13;for Doubtful Accounts&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Accounts receivable are stated at the&#13;amount management expects to collect from outstanding balances. The Company generally does not require collateral to support customer&#13;receivables. The Company provides an allowance for doubtful accounts based upon a review of the outstanding accounts receivable,&#13;historical collection information and existing economic conditions. The Company determines if receivables are past due based on&#13;days outstanding, and amounts are written off when determined to be uncollectible by management. The maximum accounting loss from&#13;the credit risk associated with accounts receivable is the amount of the receivable recorded, which is the face amount of the receivable&#13;net of the allowance for doubtful accounts. As of January 31, 2017 and 2016, the Company had reserves of $2,000.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Fair Value of Financial Instruments&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For purpose of this disclosure, the&#13;fair value of a financial instrument is the amount at which the instrument could be exchanged in a current transaction between&#13;willing parties, other than in a forced sale or liquidation. The carrying amount of the Company&amp;#8217;s short-term financial instruments&#13;approximates fair value due to the relatively short period to maturity for these instruments.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Stock Issuance Costs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Stock issuance costs are capitalized&#13;as incurred. Upon the completion of the offering, the stock issuance costs are reclassified to equity and netted against proceeds.&#13;In the event the costs are in excess of the proceeds, the costs are recorded to expense. In the case of an aborted offering, all&#13;costs are expensed. Offering costs recorded to equity for the years ended January 31, 2017 and 2016 were $0 and $678,099, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Research and Development&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Research and development is expensed&#13;as incurred. Research and development expenses for the years ended January 31, 2017 and 2016 were $144,013 and $107,632, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Shipping and Handling Costs&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company classifies freight billed&#13;to customers as sales revenue and the related freight costs as general and administrative expenses.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Revenue Recognition&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company records revenue for products&#13;when all of the following have occurred: (1) persuasive evidence of an arrangement exists, (2) the product is delivered, (3) the&#13;sales price to the customer is fixed or determinable, and (4) collectability of the related customer receivable is reasonably assured.&#13;There is no stated right of return for products.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company meets these criteria upon&#13;shipment.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cost of Sales&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Cost of sales represents costs directly&#13;related to the production and manufacturing of the Company&amp;#8217;s products. Costs include product development, freight, packaging,&#13;and print production costs.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Advertising&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Costs incurred for producing and communicating&#13;advertising for the Company are charged to operations as incurred. Producing and communicating advertising expenses for the years&#13;ended January 31, 2017 and 2016 were $1,582,048 and $2,096,026, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Stock-Based Compensation&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for stock-based&#13;compensation in accordance with ASC Topic 718, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8211; Stock Compensation&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;(&amp;#8220;ASC 718&amp;#8221;)&#13;which establishes financial accounting and reporting standards for stock-based employee compensation. It defines a fair value based&#13;method of accounting for an employee stock option or similar equity instrument. The Company accounts for compensation cost for&#13;stock option plans in accordance with ASC 718. The Company accounts for share-based payments to non-employees in accordance with&#13;ASC 505-50 &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Equity Based Payments to Non-Employees&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#8221;.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company recognizes all forms of&#13;share-based payments, including stock option grants, warrants and restricted stock grants, at their fair value on the grant date,&#13;which are based on the estimated number of awards that are ultimately expected to vest.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Share-based payments, excluding restricted&#13;stock, are valued using a Black-Scholes option pricing model. Grants of share-based payment awards issued to non-employees for&#13;services rendered have been recorded at the fair value of the share-based payment, which is the more readily determinable value.&#13;The grants are amortized on a straight-line basis over the requisite service periods, which is generally the vesting period. If&#13;an award is granted, but vesting does not occur, any previously recognized compensation cost is reversed in the period related&#13;to the termination of service. Stock-based compensation expenses are included in cost of goods sold or selling, general and administrative&#13;expenses, depending on the nature of the services provided, in the consolidated statement of operations. Share-based payments issued&#13;to placement agents are classified as a direct cost of a stock offering and are recorded as a reduction in additional paid in capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the years ended January 31, 2017&#13;and 2016, share-based compensation amounted to $598,200 and $487,316, respectively. Of the $598,200 and $487,316 recorded for the&#13;years ended January 31, 2017 and 2016, $0 and $241,769 were direct costs of a stock offering and have been recorded as a reduction&#13;in additional paid in capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The expected option term is computed&#13;using the &amp;#8220;simplified&amp;#8221; method as permitted under the provisions of ASC 718-10-S99. The Company uses the simplified&#13;method to calculate expected term of share options and similar instruments as the Company does not have sufficient historical exercise&#13;data to provide a reasonable basis upon which to estimate expected term.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The expected stock price volatility&#13;for the Company&amp;#8217;s stock options was determined by the historical volatilities for industry peers and used an average of those&#13;volatilities. Risk free interest rates were obtained from U.S. Treasury rates for the applicable periods.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Earnings (Loss) Per Share&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Earnings per share (&amp;#8220;EPS&amp;#8221;)&#13;is the amount of earnings attributable to each share of common stock. For convenience, the term is used to refer to either earnings&#13;or loss per share. EPS is computed pursuant to Section 260-10-45 of the FASB Accounting Standards Codification. Pursuant to ASC&#13;Paragraphs 260-10-45-10 through 260-10-45-16, basic EPS shall be computed by dividing income available to common stockholders (the&#13;numerator) by the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding (the denominator) during the period. Income available to&#13;common stockholders shall be computed by deducting both the dividends declared in the period on preferred stock (whether or not&#13;paid) and the dividends accumulated for the period on cumulative preferred stock (whether or not earned) from income from continuing&#13;operations (if that amount appears in the income statement) and also from net income. The computation of diluted EPS is similar&#13;to the computation of basic EPS except that the denominator is increased to include the number of additional common shares that&#13;would have been outstanding if the dilutive potential common shares had been issued during the period to reflect the potential&#13;dilution that could occur from common shares issuable through contingent shares issuance arrangement, stock options or warrants.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Pursuant to ASC Paragraphs 260-10-45-45-21&#13;through 260-10-45-45-23, diluted EPS shall be based on the most advantageous conversion rate or exercise price from the standpoint&#13;of the security holder. The dilutive effect of outstanding call options and warrants (and their equivalents) issued by the reporting&#13;entity shall be reflected in diluted EPS by application of the treasury stock method unless the provisions of Paragraphs 260-10-45-35&#13;through 45-36 and 260-10-55-8 through 55-11 require that another method be applied. Equivalents of options and warrants include&#13;non-vested stock granted to employees, stock purchase contracts, and partially paid stock subscriptions (see paragraph 260&amp;#8211;10&amp;#8211;55&amp;#8211;23).&#13;Anti-dilutive contracts, such as purchased put options and purchased call options, shall be excluded from diluted EPS. Under the&#13;treasury stock method: (a.) exercise of options and warrants shall be assumed at the beginning of the period (or at time of issuance,&#13;if later) and common shares shall be assumed to be issued, (b.) the proceeds from exercise shall be assumed to be used to purchase&#13;common stock at the average market price during the period. (See Paragraphs 260-10-45-29 and 260-10-55-4 through 55-5), and (c.)&#13;the incremental shares (the difference between the number of shares assumed issued and the number of shares assumed purchased)&#13;shall be included in the denominator of the diluted EPS computation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company had the following potential&#13;common stock equivalents at January 31, 2017:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Income taxes are provided in accordance&#13;with ASC No. 740, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Accounting for Income Taxes&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#8221;. A deferred tax asset or liability is recorded for all temporary&#13;differences between financial and tax reporting and net operating loss carryforwards. Deferred tax expense (benefit) results from&#13;the net change during the period of deferred tax assets and liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Deferred tax assets are reduced by a&#13;valuation allowance when, in the opinion of management, it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax&#13;assets will not be realized. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are adjusted for the effects of changes in tax laws and rates&#13;on the date of enactment.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company is no longer subject to&#13;tax examinations by tax authorities for years prior to 2013.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Reclassification&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Certain prior period amounts have been&#13;reclassified to conform to current period presentation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2014, the FASB issued a comprehensive&#13;new revenue recognition standard that will supersede nearly all existing revenue recognition guidance under U.S. GAAP. The standard&amp;#8217;s&#13;core principle (issued as ASU 2014-09 by the FASB), is that a company will recognize revenue when it transfers promised goods or&#13;services to customers in an amount that reflects the consideration to which the company expects to be entitled in exchange for&#13;those goods or services. These may include identifying performance obligations in the contract, estimating the amount of variable&#13;consideration to include in the transaction price and allocating the transaction price to each separate performance obligation.&#13;The new guidance must be adopted using either a full retrospective approach for all periods presented in the period of adoption&#13;or a modified retrospective approach. In August 2015, the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-14, which defers the effective date of ASU 2014-09&#13;by one year, and would allow entities the option to early adopt the new revenue standard as of the original effective date. This&#13;ASU is effective for public reporting companies for interim and annual periods beginning after December 15, 2017. The standard&#13;permits the use of either the retrospective or cumulative effect transition method. The Company has evaluated the standard and&#13;does not expect the adoption will have a material effect on its consolidated financial statements and disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2014, the FASB issued ASU 2014-15,&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Presentation&#13;of Financial Statements-Going Concern (Subtopic 205-40): Disclosure of Uncertainties about an Entity&amp;#8217;s Ability to Continue&#13;as a Going Concern.&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;ASU 2014-15 provides guidance on management&amp;#8217;s responsibility to evaluate whether there is&#13;substantial doubt about an organization&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern and to provide related footnote disclosures.&#13;For each reporting period, management will be required to evaluate whether there are conditions or events that raise substantial&#13;doubt about a company&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern within one year from the date the financial statements are&#13;issued. The amendments in ASU 2014-15 are effective for annual reporting periods ending after December 15, 2016, and for annual&#13;and interim periods thereafter. Early adoption is permitted. The Company has elected to adopt the methodologies prescribed by ASU&#13;2014-15. The adoption of ASU 2014-15 had no material effect on its financial position or results of operations.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2015, the Financial Accounting Standards&#13;Board issued Accounting Standards Update (ASU) No. 2015-03, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Interest - Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30): Simplifying&#13;the Presentation of Debt Issuance Costs&lt;/i&gt;. The amendments in this ASU require that debt issuance costs related to a recognized&#13;debt liability be presented in the balance sheet as a direct deduction from the carrying amount of that debt liability, consistent&#13;with debt discounts. The recognition and measurement guidance for debt issuance costs are not affected by the amendments in this&#13;ASU. The amendments are effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2015, and interim&#13;periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the amendments is permitted for financial statements that have not been previously&#13;issued. The amendments should be applied on a retrospective basis, wherein the balance sheet of each individual period presented&#13;should be adjusted to reflect the period-specific effects of applying the new guidance. Upon transition, an entity is required&#13;to comply with the applicable disclosures for a change in an accounting principle. These disclosures include the nature of and&#13;reason for the change in accounting principle, the transition method, a description of the prior-period information that has been&#13;retrospectively adjusted, and the effect of the change on the financial statement line items (i.e., debt issuance cost asset and&#13;the debt liability). The Company adopted ASU 2015-03 during the year ended January 31, 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2015, the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-11,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Inventory (Topic 330): Simplifying the Measurement of Inventory&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;, which modifies existing requirements regarding&#13;measuring inventory at the lower of cost or market. Under current inventory standards, the market value requires consideration&#13;of replacement cost, net realizable value and net realizable value less an approximately normal profit margin. The new guidance&#13;replaces market with net realizable value defined as estimated selling prices in the ordinary course of business, less reasonably&#13;predictable costs of completion, disposal and transportation. This eliminates the need to determine and consider replacement cost&#13;or net realizable value less an approximately normal profit margin when measuring inventory. The standard is required to be adopted&#13;for annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016, including interim periods within that annual period, which is our fiscal&#13;year 2018. The amendment is to be applied prospectively with early adoption permitted. The Company is in the process of evaluating&#13;the effect of the new guidance on its consolidated financial statements and disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-02,&#13;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Leases (Topic 842).&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;Under ASU 2016-02, lessees will be required to recognize, for all leases of 12 months or&#13;more, a liability to make lease payments and a right-of-use asset representing the right to use the underlying asset for the lease&#13;term. Additionally, the guidance requires improved disclosures to help users of financial statements better understand the nature&#13;of an entity&amp;#8217;s leasing activities. This ASU is effective for public reporting companies for interim and annual periods beginning&#13;after December 15, 2018, with early adoption permitted, and must be adopted using a modified retrospective approach. The Company&#13;is in the process of evaluating the effect of the new guidance on its consolidated financial statements and disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-09,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8211; Stock Compensation&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;(topic 718). The FASB issued this update to improve the accounting&#13;for employee share-based payments and affect all organizations that issue share-based payment awards to their employees. Several&#13;aspects of the accounting for share-based payment award transactions are simplified, including: (a) income tax consequences; (b)&#13;classification of awards as either equity or liabilities; and (c) classification on the statement of cash flows. The updated guidance&#13;is effective for annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016, including interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption&#13;of the update is permitted. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-10,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Revenue from Contracts with Customers: Identifying Performance Obligations and Licensing&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#8221; (topic 606). In March&#13;2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-08, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Revenue from Contracts with Customers: Principal versus Agent Considerations (Reporting&#13;Revenue Gross verses Net)&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;(topic 606). These amendments provide additional clarification and implementation guidance&#13;on the previously issued ASU 2014-09, &amp;#8220;Revenue from Contracts with Customers&amp;#8221;. The amendments in ASU 2016-10 provide&#13;clarifying guidance on materiality of performance obligations; evaluating distinct performance obligations; treatment of shipping&#13;and handling costs; and determining whether an entity&amp;#8217;s promise to grant a license provides a customer with either a right&#13;to use an entity&amp;#8217;s intellectual property or a right to access an entity&amp;#8217;s intellectual property. The amendments in&#13;ASU 2016-08 clarify how an entity should identify the specified good or service for the principal versus agent evaluation and how&#13;it should apply the control principle to certain types of arrangements. The adoption of ASU 2016-10 and ASU 2016-08 is to coincide&#13;with an entity&amp;#8217;s adoption of ASU 2014-09, which we intend to adopt for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after&#13;December 15, 2017. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-12,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Narrow-Scope Improvements and Practical Expedients&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;, which&#13;narrowly amended the revenue recognition guidance regarding collectability, noncash consideration, presentation of sales tax and&#13;transition and is effective during the same period as ASU 2014-09. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-15,&#13;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230): Classification of Certain Cash Receipts and Cash Payments&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt; (&amp;#8220;ASU&#13;2016-15&amp;#8221;). ASU 2016-15 will make eight targeted changes to how cash receipts and cash payments are presented and classified&#13;in the statement of cash flows. ASU 2016-15 is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2017. The new standard will&#13;require adoption on a retrospective basis unless it is impracticable to apply, in which case it would be required to apply the&#13;amendments prospectively as of the earliest date practicable. The Company is currently in the process of evaluating the impact&#13;of ASU 2016-15 on its consolidated financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In October 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-16,&#13;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Income Taxes (Topic 740): Intra-Entity Transfers of Assets Other than Inventory&amp;#8221;, &lt;/i&gt;which eliminates the exception&#13;that prohibits the recognition of current and deferred income tax effects for intra-entity transfers of assets other than inventory&#13;until the asset has been sold to an outside party. The updated guidance is effective for annual periods beginning after December&#13;15, 2019, including interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the update is permitted. The Company is currently&#13;evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In November 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-18,&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Statement&#13;of Cash Flows (Topic 230)&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;, requiring that the statement of cash flows explain the change in the total cash, cash equivalents,&#13;and amounts generally described as restricted cash or restricted cash equivalents. This guidance is effective for fiscal years,&#13;and interim reporting periods therein, beginning after December 15, 2017 with early adoption permitted. The provisions of this&#13;guidance are to be applied using a retrospective approach which requires application of the guidance for all periods presented.&#13;The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 2.25pt double; text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;1,047,455&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 4 - Investment in Meatball&#13;Obsession, LLC&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During 2011 the Company acquired a 34.62%&#13;interest in Meatball Obsession, LLC (&amp;#8220;MO&amp;#8221;) for a total investment of $27,032. This investment is accounted for using&#13;the equity method of accounting. Accordingly, investments are recorded at acquisition cost plus the Company&amp;#8217;s equity in the&#13;undistributed earnings or losses of the entity.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;At December 31, 2011 the investment&#13;was written down to $0 due to losses incurred by MO.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 5 - Related Party Transactions&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Joseph Epstein Foods&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 1, 2010, the Company entered&#13;into a five year agreement with Joseph Epstein Foods (the &amp;#8220;Manufacturer&amp;#8221;) who is a related party. The Manufacturer&#13;is co-owned by the CEO and President of the Company. The Company analyzed the relationship with the Manufacturer to determine if&#13;the Manufacturer is a variable interest entity as defined by FASB ASC 810 &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Consolidation&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;. Based on this analysis,&#13;the Company has determined that the Manufacturer is a variable interest entity but the Company is not the primary beneficiary of&#13;the variable interest entity and therefore consolidation is not required. In addition, based on the analysis the Company determined&#13;that the CEO and President of the Company is the primary beneficiary of the variable interest entity and bears the risk of loss.&#13;Under the terms of the agreement, the Company grants to the Manufacturer a revocable license to use the Company&amp;#8217;s recipes,&#13;formulas, methods and ingredients for the preparation and production of Company&amp;#8217;s products, for manufacturing the Company&amp;#8217;s&#13;product and all future improvements, modifications, substitutions and replacements developed by the Company. The Manufacturer in&#13;turn grants the Company the exclusive right to purchase the product. Under the terms of the agreement the Manufacturer agrees to&#13;manufacture, package, and store the Company&amp;#8217;s products and the Company has the right to purchase products from one or more&#13;other manufacturers, distributors or suppliers. In September 2016, the agreement was amended and restated to extend the agreement&#13;until August 2, 2021. The amended agreement contains a perpetual automatic renewal clause for a period of one year after the expiration&#13;of the initial term. During the renewal period either party may cancel the contract with written notice nine months prior to the&#13;termination date. The term of this Agreement shall expire on the later of the expiration date or a date which is three (3) years&#13;following a Change of Control. For purposes of the agreement, a Change of Control shall occur when a third party who is not currently&#13;a shareholder of the Company acquires control of at least fifty-one percent (51%) of the voting shares of the Company.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Under the terms of the agreement if the Company&#13;specifies any change in packaging or shipping materials which results in the manufacturer incurring increased expense for packaging&#13;and shipping materials or in the Manufacturer being unable to utilize obsolete packaging or shipping materials in ordinary packaging&#13;or shipping, the Company agrees to pay as additional product cost the additional cost for packaging and shipping materials and&#13;to purchase at cost such obsolete packaging and shipping materials. If the Company requests any repackaging of the product, other&#13;than due to defects in the original packaging, the Company will reimburse the Manufacturer for any labor costs incurred in repackaging.&#13;Per the agreement, all product delivery shipping costs are the expense of the Company. The Company agreed with the Manufacturer&#13;at the end of the last fiscal year that Company would purchase a minimum of $963,000 of product each month and that any amount&#13;below that sum would be a charge of 12% of that shortfall each month. In return, the Manufacturer obligated itself to offer the&#13;Company competitive prices and would not co-pack for other suppliers and would either maintain or lower its payable to the Company&#13;each quarter. In addition, the Manufacturer agreed to rebate the Company any overage of gross margin above 12% each month.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;From time to time the Company will make investments&#13;in equipment located at the Manufacturer&amp;#8217;s facility. The equipment is capitalized and depreciated by the Company over the&#13;estimated useful life.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

The Company is required to prepay the note 10% of the net proceeds&#13;received upon the closing of a capital raise, except for, those transactions conducted with the Company&amp;#8217;s Chief Executive&#13;Officer. The Company paid $248,373 toward the outstanding balance, a portion of which is 10% of the net proceeds from the final&#13;closing of the private placement in November 2015.  Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 7 - Loan and Security Agreement&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

EGC may from time to time make loans in an aggregate amount not to exceed the Inventory&#13;Revolving Line of Credit against Eligible Inventory (as defined in the Loan and Security Agreement) in an amount up to 50% of finished&#13;goods and in an amount up to 20% of raw material.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The revolving interest rates is equal&#13;to the highest prime rate in effect during each month as generally reported by Citibank, N.A. plus (a) 2.5% on loans and advances&#13;made against eligible accounts and (b) 4.0% on loans made against eligible inventory. The term loan bears interest at a rate of&#13;the highest prime rate in effect during each month as generally reported by Citibank, N.A. plus 4.0%. The initial term of the facility&#13;is for a period of two years and will automatically renew for an additional one year period. The Company is required to pay an&#13;annual facility fee equal to 0.75% of the total $3,200,000 facility and pays an annualized maintenance fee equal to 2.16% of the&#13;total facility. In the event of default, the Company shall pay 10% above the stated rates of interest per the Agreement. The drawdowns&#13;are secured by all of the assets of the Company.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the first quarter of 2016, the&#13;Company adopted ASU 2015-03, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Interest &amp;#8211; Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30): Simplifying the Presentation&#13;of Debt Issuance Costs&lt;/i&gt;. &amp;#8220;In accordance with the guidance, $26,620 of unamortized debt issuance costs, specifically attributable&#13;to each of the Company&amp;#8217;s debt issuances, were reclassified from other assets, as previously reported on the Consolidated&#13;Balance Sheet as of January 31, 2016, to line of credit, net. The unamortized debt issuance costs are now presented as a direct&#13;deduction from each debt liability, consistent with the presentation of the corresponding debt discount, where applicable.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The debt discount will be amortized&#13;over the earlier of (i) the term of the debt or (ii) conversion of the debt, using the straight-line method which approximates&#13;the effective interest method. The amortization of debt discount is included as a component of other expense in the consolidated&#13;statements of operations. There was unamortized debt discount of $0 and $26,620 as of January 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;As of January 31, 2017 and 2016 the&#13;outstanding balance on the line of credit was $1,363,145 and $959,621, respectively. Due to the terms of the agreement regarding&#13;a subjective acceleration clause and a lockbox arrangement, the line of credit is shown as a current liability on the consolidated&#13;balance sheets.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On September 3, 2014, the Company also&#13;entered into a 5 year $600,000 Secured Promissory Note (&amp;#8220;EGC Note&amp;#8221;) with EGC. In September 2016, the ECG Note was increased&#13;to $700,000 with an extended maturity date of September 30, 2021. The amended EGC Note is payable in 60 monthly installments of&#13;$11,667. The EGC Note bears interest at the prime rate plus 4.0% and is payable monthly, in arrears. In the event of default, the&#13;Company shall pay 10% above the stated rates of interest per the Loan and Security Agreement. The EGC Note is secured by all of&#13;the assets of the Company. The outstanding balance on the term loan was $653,332 and $440,000 as of January 31, 2017 and 2016,&#13;respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On December 19, 2014, the Company entered&#13;into a securities purchase agreement (the &amp;#8220;Manatuck Purchase Agreement&amp;#8221;) with Manatuck Hill Partners, LLC (&amp;#8220;Manatuck&amp;#8221;)&#13;whereby the Company issued a convertible redeemable debenture (the &amp;#8220;Manatuck Debenture&amp;#8221;) in favor of Manatuck. The&#13;Manatuck Debenture is for $2,000,000 bearing interest at a rate of 14% and matures in February 2016. Upon issuance of the Manatuck&#13;Debenture, the Company granted Manatuck 200,000 shares of the Company&amp;#8217;s restricted common stock. In April 2015, the maturity&#13;date was extended to May 2016 and 30,000 shares of restricted common stock were issued to Manatuck. Based on management&amp;#8217;s&#13;review, the accounting for debt modification applied. The Company valued the 30,000 shares at the grant date share price of $1.32&#13;and recorded $39,600 to debt discount on the consolidated balance sheet.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Upon issuance of the debenture and subsequent&#13;extension, a debt discount of $498,350 was recorded for the fees incurred by the buyer as well as the value of the common shares&#13;granted to Manatuck. The debt discount will be amortized over the earlier of (i) the term of the debt or (ii) conversion of the&#13;debt, using the straight-line method which approximates the effective interest method. The amortization of debt discount is included&#13;as a component of other expense in the consolidated statements of operations.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On October 29, 2015, the note was further&#13;amended to extend the maturity date to December 19, 2016. Per the terms of the execution of the extension, the Company was required&#13;to purchase the above 230,000 shares issued to Manatuck for a share price of $0.65, a value of $149,500 and incurred an amendment&#13;fee of $170,500, both of which were added to the outstanding principal of the debt. In addition, the extension reduced accrued&#13;interest by $220,000 and increased the outstanding principal of the debt by $220,000. Based on management&amp;#8217;s review, the accounting&#13;for debt extinguishment applied. In accordance with the accounting for debt extinguishment, the Company wrote-off the existing&#13;debt of $2,000,000, wrote-off the unamortized debt discount of $190,483 and wrote-off the remaining debt issuance costs relating&#13;to this note of $19,106. The loss on debt extinguishment of $380,089 on the statement of operations is comprised of the write-off&#13;of the remaining debt discount of $190,483, the write-off of the debt issuance costs of $19,106, and the amendment fee of $170,500.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

The principal amount&#13;of the note was increased to $2,898,523, which is inclusive of accrued interest payable through October 31, 2016. In addition,&#13;the Company paid an origination fee of $50,000 on October 31, 2016 which is recorded as a debt discount and will be amortized over&#13;the remaining life of the note using the effective interest method.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 10 - Stockholders&amp;#8217;&#13;Equity&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;(A) Series A Convertible Preferred&#13;Stock Transactions&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On May 28, 2015, the Company amended&#13;its articles of incorporation to establish the designation, powers, rights, privileges, preferences and restrictions of the Series&#13;A Convertible Preferred Stock (&amp;#8220;Series A Preferred&amp;#8221;). The Company authorized 120,000 shares of Series A Preferred with&#13;each share of our Series A Preferred having a par value of $0.00001 and stated value equal to $100, as adjusted for stock dividends,&#13;combinations, splits and certain other events. The Company analyzed the conversion feature for potential derivative classification.&#13;On May 28, 2015, the Company amended its articles of incorporation to establish the designation, powers, rights, privileges, preferences&#13;and restrictions of the Series A Convertible Preferred Stock (&amp;#8220;Series A Preferred&amp;#8221;). The Company authorized 120,000&#13;shares of Series A Preferred with each share of our Series A Preferred having a par value of $0.00001 and stated value equal to&#13;$100 (&amp;#8220;Stated Value&amp;#8221;), as adjusted for stock dividends, combinations, splits and certain other events. The Company&#13;analyzed the conversion feature for potential derivative classification. Despite the ratchet features included in the conversion&#13;option, the Company concluded that equity treatment was warranted since the feature was clearly and closely related to the host&#13;contract. The holders of the Series Preferred A will be entitled to (a) dividends at a rate of 8% per annum, (b) a liquidation&#13;preference equal to $0.675 per Series A Preferred share, (c) the option to convert the Series A Preferred shares to a number of&#13;shares of common stock calculated by dividing the Stated Value by $0.675 and (d) warrants to purchase a number of common shares&#13;calculated by dividing the Stated Value by $0.675 exercisable for a period of five years at a price of $1.00 per share. There is&#13;also an automatic conversion based on the occurrence of certain events detailed in the Certificate of Designation. As of January&#13;31, 2017, all accrued dividends had been paid in Company common stock. Additionally, in April 2016 the Company granted an aggregate&#13;of an additional 2,510,001 Warrants to investors in a prior offering. These Warrants are for a term of five (5) years at an exercise&#13;price of $1.50 per share.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During May 2015, six directors of the Company&#13;entered into convertible note agreements with a maturity date of July 22, 2016 for total proceeds to the Company of $650,000. In&#13;June 2015, the notes were converted into Series A Preferred. Additional proceeds of $560,000 were received pursuant to closings&#13;that occurred in June, August and September. In connection with the closings, the Company also granted warrants to purchase 1,481,481&#13;and 179,259 shares of common stock at $0.675 per share to shareholders and the placement agent, respectively. The warrants granted&#13;to the placement agent have a grant date fair value of $84,547 which is treated as a direct cost of the Financing and has been&#13;recorded as a reduction in additional paid in capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During November 2015, the Company completed&#13;the final closing of a private placement with 11 accredited investors and issued an aggregate of 10,200 shares of Series A Preferred&#13;and warrants to purchase 1,511,112 shares of common stock for aggregate gross proceeds to the Company of $1,020,000. Stock issuance&#13;costs of $132,600 were paid to placement agents yielding net proceeds of $887,400. Of these issuance costs, approximately $86,000&#13;were pursuant to the promissory note agreement as discussed in Note 6.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Note 11 - Commitments and Contingencies&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Litigations, Claims and Assessments&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;From time to time, the Company may become&#13;involved in various lawsuits and legal proceedings, which arise in the ordinary course of business. Litigation is subject to inherent&#13;uncertainties, and an adverse result in these or other matters may arise from time to time that may harm its business. The Company&#13;is currently not aware of any such legal proceedings or claims that they believe will have, individually or in the aggregate, a&#13;material adverse effect on its business, financial condition or operating results.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Licensing and Royalty Agreements&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 1, 2010, the Company was assigned&#13;a Development and License agreement (the &amp;#8220;Agreement&amp;#8221;). Under the terms of the Agreement the Licensor shall develop&#13;for the Company a line of beef meatballs with sauce, turkey meatballs with sauce and other similar meats and sauces for commercial&#13;manufacture, distribution and sale (each a &amp;#8220;Licensor Product&amp;#8221; and collectively the &amp;#8220;Licensor Products&amp;#8221;).&#13;Licensor shall work with Licensee to develop Licensor Products that are acceptable to Licensee. Upon acceptance of a Licensor Product&#13;by Licensee, Licensor&amp;#8217;s trade secret recipes, formulas methods and ingredients for the preparation and production of such&#13;Licensor Products (the &amp;#8220;Recipes&amp;#8221;) shall be subject to this Development and License Agreement.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The term of the Agreement (the &amp;#8220;Term&amp;#8221;)&#13;shall consist of the Exclusive Term and the Non-Exclusive Term. The 12-month period beginning on each January 1 and ending on each&#13;December 31 is referred to herein as an &amp;#8220;Agreement Year&amp;#8221;.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Exclusive Term began on January&#13;1, 2009 (the &amp;#8220;Effective Date&amp;#8221;) and ends on the 50th anniversary of the Effective Date, unless terminated or extended&#13;as provided herein. Licensor, at its option, may terminate the Exclusive Term by notice in writing to Licensee, delivered between&#13;the 60th and the 90th day following the end of any Agreement Year if, on or before the 60th day following the end of such Agreement&#13;Year, Licensee has not paid Licensor Royalties with respect to such Agreement Year at least equal to the minimum royalty (the &amp;#8220;Minimum&#13;Royalty&amp;#8221;) for such Agreement Year. Subject to the foregoing sentence, and provided Licensee has not breached this Agreement&#13;and failed to cure such breach in accordance herewith, Licensee may extend the Exclusive Term for an additional twenty five (25)&#13;years, by notice in writing to Licensor, delivered on or before the 50th anniversary of the Effective Date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Non-Exclusive Term begins upon expiration&#13;of the Exclusive Term and continues indefinitely thereafter, until terminated by Licensor due to a material breach hereof by Licensee&#13;that remains uncured after notice and opportunity to cure in accordance herewith, or until terminated by Licensee.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Either party may terminate this Agreement&#13;in the event that the other party materially breaches its obligations and fails to cure such material breach within sixty (60)&#13;days following written notice from the non-breaching party specifying the nature of the breach. The following termination rights&#13;are in addition to the termination rights provided elsewhere in the agreement.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse&gt;&#13;&lt;tr&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 24px; font: 11pt/115% Calibri
 Helvetica
 Sans-Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: top; width: 24px; font: 11pt/115% Calibri
 Helvetica
 Sans-Serif&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;&amp;#9679;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=font: 11pt/115% Calibri
 Helvetica
 Sans-Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;Termination by Licensee - Licensee shall have the right to terminate this Agreement at any time on sixty (60) days written notice to Licensor. In such event, all moneys paid to Licensor shall be deemed non-refundable.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Under the terms of the Agreement the&#13;Company is required to pay quarterly royalty fees as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the Exclusive Term and the Non-Exclusive&#13;Term the Company will pay a royalty equal to the royalty rate (the &amp;#8220;Royalty Rate&amp;#8221;), multiplied by Company&amp;#8217;s &amp;#8220;Net&#13;Sales&amp;#8221;. As used herein, &amp;#8220;Net Sales&amp;#8221; means gross invoiced sales of Products, directly or indirectly to unrelated&#13;third parties, less (a) discounts (including cash discounts), and retroactive price reductions or allowances actually allowed or&#13;granted from the billed amount (collectively &amp;#8220;Discounts&amp;#8221;); (b) credits, rebates, and allowances actually granted upon&#13;claims, rejections or returns, including recalls (voluntary or otherwise) (collectively, &amp;#8220;Credits&amp;#8221;); (c) freight, postage,&#13;shipping and insurance charges; (d) taxes, duties or other governmental charges levied on or measured by the billing amount, when&#13;included in billing, as adjusted for rebates and refunds; and (e) provisions for uncollectible accounts determined in accordance&#13;with reasonable accounting methods, consistently applied.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Royalty Rate shall be: 6% of net&#13;sales up to $500,000 of net sales for each Agreement year; 4% of Net Sales from $500,000 up to $2,500,000 of Net Sales for each&#13;Agreement year; 2% of Net Sales from $2,500,000 up to $20,000,000 of Net Sales for each Agreement year; and 1% of Net Sales in&#13;excess of $20,000,000 of Net Sales for each Agreement year.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In order to continue the Exclusive term,&#13;the Company shall pay a minimum royalty with respect to the preceding Agreement year as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
