 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Agreements with Placement Agents&#13;and Finders&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.25in&gt;(A) April 1, 2015&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company entered into a fourth Financial&#13;Advisory and Investment Banking Agreement with Spartan Capital Securities, LLC (&amp;#8220;Spartan&amp;#8221;) effective April 1, 2015&#13;(the &amp;#8220;Spartan Advisory Agreement&amp;#8221;). Pursuant to the Spartan Advisory Agreement, the Company shall pay to Spartan a&#13;non-refundable monthly fee of $10,000 through October 1, 2015. The monthly fee shall survive any termination of the Agreement.&#13;Additionally, (i) if at least $4,000,000 is raised in the Financing, the Company shall pay to Spartan a non-refundable fee of $5,000&#13;per month from November 1, 2015 through October 2017; and (ii) if at least $5,000,000 is raised in the Financing, the Company shall&#13;pay to Spartan a non-refundable fee of $5,000 per month from November 1, 2017 through October 2019. If $10,000,000 or more is raised&#13;in the Financing, the Company shall issue to Spartan shares of its common stock having an aggregate value of $5,000 (as determined&#13;by reference to the average volume weighted average trading price for the last five trading days of the immediately preceding month)&#13;on the first day of each month during the period from November 1, 2015 through October 1, 2019.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company upon closing of the Financing&#13;shall pay consideration to Spartan, in cash, a fee in an amount equal to 10% of the aggregate gross proceeds raised in the Financing&#13;and 3% of the aggregate gross proceeds raised in the Financing for expenses incurred by Spartan. The Company shall grant and deliver&#13;to Spartan at the closing of the Financing, for nominal consideration, five year warrants to purchase a number of shares of the&#13;Company&amp;#8217;s common stock equal to 10% of the number of shares of common stock (and/or shares of common stock issuable upon&#13;exercise of securities or upon conversion or exchange of convertible or exchangeable securities) sold at such closing. The warrants&#13;shall be exercisable at any time during the five year period commencing on the closing to which they relate at an exercise price&#13;equal to the purchase price per share of common stock paid by investors in the Financing or, in the case of exercisable, convertible,&#13;or exchangeable securities, the exercise, conversion or exchange price thereof. If the Financing is consummated by means of more&#13;than one closing, Spartan shall be entitled to the fees provided herein with respect to each such closing.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the year ended January 31, 2016,&#13;the Company paid to Spartan a one-time engagement fee of $10,000. In connection with the Initial Closing, the Company agreed to&#13;pay an aggregate cash fee and non-accountable allowance of $157,300. The Company also granted warrants to purchase 179,259 shares&#13;of common stock at $0.675 per share. The warrants have a grant date fair value of $84,547 which is treated as a direct cost of&#13;the Financing and has been recorded as a reduction in additional paid in capital. During the year ended January 31, 2017, no payments&#13;were made to Spartan.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The preparation of consolidated financial&#13;statements in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions&#13;that affect the amounts reported in the consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Such estimates and assumptions&#13;impact, among others, the following: allowance for doubtful accounts, inventory obsolescence and the fair value of share-based&#13;payments.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Revenue Recognition&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company records revenue for products&#13;when all of the following have occurred: (1) persuasive evidence of an arrangement exists, (2) the product is delivered, (3) the&#13;sales price to the customer is fixed or determinable, and (4) collectability of the related customer receivable is reasonably assured.&#13;There is no stated right of return for products.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company meets these criteria upon&#13;shipment.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Expenses such as slotting fees, sales&#13;discounts, and allowances are accounted for as a direct reduction of revenues as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Advertising&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman

&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Stock-Based Compensation&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for stock-based&#13;compensation in accordance with ASC Topic 718, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8211; Stock Compensation&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;(&amp;#8220;ASC 718&amp;#8221;)&#13;which establishes financial accounting and reporting standards for stock-based employee compensation. It defines a fair value based&#13;method of accounting for an employee stock option or similar equity instrument. The Company accounts for compensation cost for&#13;stock option plans in accordance with ASC 718. The Company accounts for share-based payments to non-employees in accordance with&#13;ASC 505-50 &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Equity Based Payments to Non-Employees&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#8221;.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company recognizes all forms of&#13;share-based payments, including stock option grants, warrants and restricted stock grants, at their fair value on the grant date,&#13;which are based on the estimated number of awards that are ultimately expected to vest.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Share-based payments, excluding restricted&#13;stock, are valued using a Black-Scholes option pricing model. Grants of share-based payment awards issued to non-employees for&#13;services rendered have been recorded at the fair value of the share-based payment, which is the more readily determinable value.&#13;The grants are amortized on a straight-line basis over the requisite service periods, which is generally the vesting period. If&#13;an award is granted, but vesting does not occur, any previously recognized compensation cost is reversed in the period related&#13;to the termination of service. Stock-based compensation expenses are included in cost of goods sold or selling, general and administrative&#13;expenses, depending on the nature of the services provided, in the consolidated statement of operations. Share-based payments issued&#13;to placement agents are classified as a direct cost of a stock offering and are recorded as a reduction in additional paid in capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the years ended January 31, 2017&#13;and 2016, share-based compensation amounted to $598,200 and $487,316, respectively. Of the $598,200 and $487,316 recorded for the&#13;years ended January 31, 2017 and 2016, $0 and $241,769 were direct costs of a stock offering and have been recorded as a reduction&#13;in additional paid in capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For the years ended January 31, 2017&#13;and 2016, when computing fair value of share-based payments, the Company has considered the following variables:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif&gt;%&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The expected option term is computed&#13;using the &amp;#8220;simplified&amp;#8221; method as permitted under the provisions of ASC 718-10-S99. The Company uses the simplified&#13;method to calculate expected term of share options and similar instruments as the Company does not have sufficient historical exercise&#13;data to provide a reasonable basis upon which to estimate expected term.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Earnings (Loss) Per Share&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Earnings per share (&amp;#8220;EPS&amp;#8221;)&#13;is the amount of earnings attributable to each share of common stock. For convenience, the term is used to refer to either earnings&#13;or loss per share. EPS is computed pursuant to Section 260-10-45 of the FASB Accounting Standards Codification. Pursuant to ASC&#13;Paragraphs 260-10-45-10 through 260-10-45-16, basic EPS shall be computed by dividing income available to common stockholders (the&#13;numerator) by the weighted-average number of common shares outstanding (the denominator) during the period. Income available to&#13;common stockholders shall be computed by deducting both the dividends declared in the period on preferred stock (whether or not&#13;paid) and the dividends accumulated for the period on cumulative preferred stock (whether or not earned) from income from continuing&#13;operations (if that amount appears in the income statement) and also from net income. The computation of diluted EPS is similar&#13;to the computation of basic EPS except that the denominator is increased to include the number of additional common shares that&#13;would have been outstanding if the dilutive potential common shares had been issued during the period to reflect the potential&#13;dilution that could occur from common shares issuable through contingent shares issuance arrangement, stock options or warrants.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Pursuant to ASC Paragraphs 260-10-45-45-21&#13;through 260-10-45-45-23, diluted EPS shall be based on the most advantageous conversion rate or exercise price from the standpoint&#13;of the security holder. The dilutive effect of outstanding call options and warrants (and their equivalents) issued by the reporting&#13;entity shall be reflected in diluted EPS by application of the treasury stock method unless the provisions of Paragraphs 260-10-45-35&#13;through 45-36 and 260-10-55-8 through 55-11 require that another method be applied. Equivalents of options and warrants include&#13;non-vested stock granted to employees, stock purchase contracts, and partially paid stock subscriptions (see paragraph 260&amp;#8211;10&amp;#8211;55&amp;#8211;23).&#13;Anti-dilutive contracts, such as purchased put options and purchased call options, shall be excluded from diluted EPS. Under the&#13;treasury stock method: (a.) exercise of options and warrants shall be assumed at the beginning of the period (or at time of issuance,&#13;if later) and common shares shall be assumed to be issued, (b.) the proceeds from exercise shall be assumed to be used to purchase&#13;common stock at the average market price during the period. (See Paragraphs 260-10-45-29 and 260-10-55-4 through 55-5), and (c.)&#13;the incremental shares (the difference between the number of shares assumed issued and the number of shares assumed purchased)&#13;shall be included in the denominator of the diluted EPS computation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company had the following potential&#13;common stock equivalents at January 31, 2017:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif&gt;&lt;b&gt;Total common stock equivalents&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 2.25pt double; text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;8,927,805&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Income taxes are provided in accordance&#13;with ASC No. 740, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Accounting for Income Taxes&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#8221;. A deferred tax asset or liability is recorded for all temporary&#13;differences between financial and tax reporting and net operating loss carryforwards. Deferred tax expense (benefit) results from&#13;the net change during the period of deferred tax assets and liabilities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Deferred tax assets are reduced by a&#13;valuation allowance when, in the opinion of management, it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax&#13;assets will not be realized. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are adjusted for the effects of changes in tax laws and rates&#13;on the date of enactment.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Reclassification&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2014, the FASB issued a comprehensive&#13;new revenue recognition standard that will supersede nearly all existing revenue recognition guidance under U.S. GAAP. The standard&amp;#8217;s&#13;core principle (issued as ASU 2014-09 by the FASB), is that a company will recognize revenue when it transfers promised goods or&#13;services to customers in an amount that reflects the consideration to which the company expects to be entitled in exchange for&#13;those goods or services. These may include identifying performance obligations in the contract, estimating the amount of variable&#13;consideration to include in the transaction price and allocating the transaction price to each separate performance obligation.&#13;The new guidance must be adopted using either a full retrospective approach for all periods presented in the period of adoption&#13;or a modified retrospective approach. In August 2015, the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-14, which defers the effective date of ASU 2014-09&#13;by one year, and would allow entities the option to early adopt the new revenue standard as of the original effective date. This&#13;ASU is effective for public reporting companies for interim and annual periods beginning after December 15, 2017. The standard&#13;permits the use of either the retrospective or cumulative effect transition method. The Company has evaluated the standard and&#13;does not expect the adoption will have a material effect on its consolidated financial statements and disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2014, the FASB issued ASU 2014-15,&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Presentation&#13;of Financial Statements-Going Concern (Subtopic 205-40): Disclosure of Uncertainties about an Entity&amp;#8217;s Ability to Continue&#13;as a Going Concern.&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;ASU 2014-15 provides guidance on management&amp;#8217;s responsibility to evaluate whether there is&#13;substantial doubt about an organization&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern and to provide related footnote disclosures.&#13;For each reporting period, management will be required to evaluate whether there are conditions or events that raise substantial&#13;doubt about a company&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern within one year from the date the financial statements are&#13;issued. The amendments in ASU 2014-15 are effective for annual reporting periods ending after December 15, 2016, and for annual&#13;and interim periods thereafter. Early adoption is permitted. The Company has elected to adopt the methodologies prescribed by ASU&#13;2014-15. The adoption of ASU 2014-15 had no material effect on its financial position or results of operations.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2015, the Financial Accounting Standards&#13;Board issued Accounting Standards Update (ASU) No. 2015-03, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Interest - Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30): Simplifying&#13;the Presentation of Debt Issuance Costs&lt;/i&gt;. The amendments in this ASU require that debt issuance costs related to a recognized&#13;debt liability be presented in the balance sheet as a direct deduction from the carrying amount of that debt liability, consistent&#13;with debt discounts. The recognition and measurement guidance for debt issuance costs are not affected by the amendments in this&#13;ASU. The amendments are effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2015, and interim&#13;periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the amendments is permitted for financial statements that have not been previously&#13;issued. The amendments should be applied on a retrospective basis, wherein the balance sheet of each individual period presented&#13;should be adjusted to reflect the period-specific effects of applying the new guidance. Upon transition, an entity is required&#13;to comply with the applicable disclosures for a change in an accounting principle. These disclosures include the nature of and&#13;reason for the change in accounting principle, the transition method, a description of the prior-period information that has been&#13;retrospectively adjusted, and the effect of the change on the financial statement line items (i.e., debt issuance cost asset and&#13;the debt liability). The Company adopted ASU 2015-03 during the year ended January 31, 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2015, the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-11,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Inventory (Topic 330): Simplifying the Measurement of Inventory&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;, which modifies existing requirements regarding&#13;measuring inventory at the lower of cost or market. Under current inventory standards, the market value requires consideration&#13;of replacement cost, net realizable value and net realizable value less an approximately normal profit margin. The new guidance&#13;replaces market with net realizable value defined as estimated selling prices in the ordinary course of business, less reasonably&#13;predictable costs of completion, disposal and transportation. This eliminates the need to determine and consider replacement cost&#13;or net realizable value less an approximately normal profit margin when measuring inventory. The standard is required to be adopted&#13;for annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016, including interim periods within that annual period, which is our fiscal&#13;year 2018. The amendment is to be applied prospectively with early adoption permitted. The Company is in the process of evaluating&#13;the effect of the new guidance on its consolidated financial statements and disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-02,&#13;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Leases (Topic 842).&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;Under ASU 2016-02, lessees will be required to recognize, for all leases of 12 months or&#13;more, a liability to make lease payments and a right-of-use asset representing the right to use the underlying asset for the lease&#13;term. Additionally, the guidance requires improved disclosures to help users of financial statements better understand the nature&#13;of an entity&amp;#8217;s leasing activities. This ASU is effective for public reporting companies for interim and annual periods beginning&#13;after December 15, 2018, with early adoption permitted, and must be adopted using a modified retrospective approach. The Company&#13;is in the process of evaluating the effect of the new guidance on its consolidated financial statements and disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-09,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8211; Stock Compensation&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;(topic 718). The FASB issued this update to improve the accounting&#13;for employee share-based payments and affect all organizations that issue share-based payment awards to their employees. Several&#13;aspects of the accounting for share-based payment award transactions are simplified, including: (a) income tax consequences; (b)&#13;classification of awards as either equity or liabilities; and (c) classification on the statement of cash flows. The updated guidance&#13;is effective for annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016, including interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption&#13;of the update is permitted. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: center&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-10,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Revenue from Contracts with Customers: Identifying Performance Obligations and Licensing&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#8221; (topic 606). In March&#13;2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-08, &amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Revenue from Contracts with Customers: Principal versus Agent Considerations (Reporting&#13;Revenue Gross verses Net)&amp;#8221; &lt;/i&gt;(topic 606). These amendments provide additional clarification and implementation guidance&#13;on the previously issued ASU 2014-09, &amp;#8220;Revenue from Contracts with Customers&amp;#8221;. The amendments in ASU 2016-10 provide&#13;clarifying guidance on materiality of performance obligations; evaluating distinct performance obligations; treatment of shipping&#13;and handling costs; and determining whether an entity&amp;#8217;s promise to grant a license provides a customer with either a right&#13;to use an entity&amp;#8217;s intellectual property or a right to access an entity&amp;#8217;s intellectual property. The amendments in&#13;ASU 2016-08 clarify how an entity should identify the specified good or service for the principal versus agent evaluation and how&#13;it should apply the control principle to certain types of arrangements. The adoption of ASU 2016-10 and ASU 2016-08 is to coincide&#13;with an entity&amp;#8217;s adoption of ASU 2014-09, which we intend to adopt for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after&#13;December 15, 2017. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-12,&#13;&amp;#8220;&lt;i&gt;Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606): Narrow-Scope Improvements and Practical Expedients&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;, which&#13;narrowly amended the revenue recognition guidance regarding collectability, noncash consideration, presentation of sales tax and&#13;transition and is effective during the same period as ASU 2014-09. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-15,&#13;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230): Classification of Certain Cash Receipts and Cash Payments&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt; (&amp;#8220;ASU&#13;2016-15&amp;#8221;). ASU 2016-15 will make eight targeted changes to how cash receipts and cash payments are presented and classified&#13;in the statement of cash flows. ASU 2016-15 is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2017. The new standard will&#13;require adoption on a retrospective basis unless it is impracticable to apply, in which case it would be required to apply the&#13;amendments prospectively as of the earliest date practicable. The Company is currently in the process of evaluating the impact&#13;of ASU 2016-15 on its consolidated financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In October 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-16,&#13;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Income Taxes (Topic 740): Intra-Entity Transfers of Assets Other than Inventory&amp;#8221;, &lt;/i&gt;which eliminates the exception&#13;that prohibits the recognition of current and deferred income tax effects for intra-entity transfers of assets other than inventory&#13;until the asset has been sold to an outside party. The updated guidance is effective for annual periods beginning after December&#13;15, 2019, including interim periods within those fiscal years. Early adoption of the update is permitted. The Company is currently&#13;evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In November 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-18,&lt;i&gt;&amp;#8220;Statement&#13;of Cash Flows (Topic 230)&amp;#8221;&lt;/i&gt;, requiring that the statement of cash flows explain the change in the total cash, cash equivalents,&#13;and amounts generally described as restricted cash or restricted cash equivalents. This guidance is effective for fiscal years,&#13;and interim reporting periods therein, beginning after December 15, 2017 with early adoption permitted. The provisions of this&#13;guidance are to be applied using a retrospective approach which requires application of the guidance for all periods presented.&#13;The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the new standard.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=margin: 0pt&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;. Inventory was comprised of the following&#13;at January 31, 2017 and 2016:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 11pt Calibri

 Serif&gt;&lt;b&gt;January 31, 2017&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=border-bottom: black 1.5pt solid; text-align: center; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;&lt;b&gt;Change in valuation allowance&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1.5pt solid; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1.5pt solid; text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;211,139&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1.5pt solid; line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 1.5pt solid; text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;1,405,640&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: white&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif&gt;&lt;b&gt;Income tax provision (benefit)&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 2.25pt double; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 2.25pt double; text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;-&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 2.25pt double; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: black 2.25pt double; text-align: right; line-height: 115%&gt;&lt;font style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;-&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=line-height: 115%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has U.S. federal net operating&#13;loss carryovers (NOLs) of approximately $12.9M and $12.6M at January 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively, available to offset taxable&#13;income through 2034. If not used, these NOLs may be subject to limitation under Internal Revenue Code Section 382 should there&#13;be a greater than 50% ownership change as determined under the regulations. The Company plans on undertaking a detailed analysis&#13;of any historical and/or current Section 382 ownership changes that may limit the utilization of the net operating loss carryovers.&#13;The Company also has New Jersey State Net Operating Loss carry overs of $12.9M and $12.6M at January 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively,&#13;available to offset future taxable income through 2035.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In assessing the realization of deferred&#13;tax assets, management considers whether it is more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will not&#13;be realized. The ultimate realization of deferred tax assets is dependent upon future generation for taxable income during the&#13;periods in which temporary differences representing net future deductible amounts become deductible. Management considers the scheduled&#13;reversal of deferred tax liabilities, projected future taxable income and tax planning strategies in making this assessment. After&#13;consideration of all the information available, Management believes that significant uncertainty exists with respect to future&#13;realization of the deferred tax assets and has therefore established a full valuation allowance. For the years ended January 31,&#13;2017 and 2016, the change in the valuation allowance was $211,139 and $1,405,640.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company evaluated the provisions&#13;of ASC 740 related to the accounting for uncertainty in income taxes recognized in an enterprise&amp;#8217;s financial statements.&#13;ASC 740 prescribes a comprehensive model for how a company should recognize, present, and disclose uncertain positions that the&#13;Company has taken or expects to take in its tax return. For those benefits to be recognized, a tax position must be more-likely-than-not&#13;to be sustained upon examination by taxing authorities. Differences between tax positions taken or expected to be taken in a tax&#13;return and the net benefit recognized and measured pursuant to the interpretation are referred to as &amp;#8220;unrecognized benefits.&amp;#8221;&#13;A liability is recognized (or amount of net operating loss carry forward or amount of tax refundable is reduced) for unrecognized&#13;tax benefit because it represents an enterprise&amp;#8217;s potential future obligation to the taxing authority for a tax position&#13;that was not recognized as a result of applying the provisions of ASC 740.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;If applicable, interest costs related&#13;to the unrecognized tax benefits are required to be calculated and would be classified as &amp;#8220;Other expenses &amp;#8211; Interest&amp;#8221;&#13;in the statement of operations. Penalties would be recognized as a component of &amp;#8220;General and administrative.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;No interest or penalties on unpaid tax&#13;were recorded during the years ended January 31, 2017 and 2016, respectively. As of January 31, 2017 and 2016, no liability for&#13;unrecognized tax benefits was required to be reported. The Company does not expect any significant changes in its unrecognized&#13;tax benefits in the next year.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt/normal Times New Roman
 Times

var Show = {};
Show.LastAR = null
Show.hideAR = function(){
	Show.LastAR.style.display = 'none';
};
Show.showAR = function ( link
 id
 win ){
	if( Show.LastAR ){
		Show.hideAR();
	}
	var ref = link;
	do {
		ref = ref.nextSibling;
	} while (ref && ref.nodeName != 'TABLE');
	if (!ref || ref.nodeName != 'TABLE') {
		var tmp = win ?
			win.document.getElementById(id) :
			document.getElementById(id);
		if( tmp ){
			ref = tmp.cloneNode(true);
			ref.id = '';
			link.parentNode.appendChild(ref);
		}
	}
	if( ref ){
		ref.style.display = 'block';
		Show.LastAR = ref;
	}
};
Show.toggleNext = function( link ){
	var ref = link;
	do{
		ref = ref.nextSibling;
	}while( ref.nodeName != 'DIV' );
	if( ref.style &&
		ref.style.display &&
		ref.style.display == 'none' ){
		ref.style.display = 'block';
		if( link.textContent ){
			link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '+'
 '-' );
		}else{
			link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '+'
 '-' );
		}
	}else{
		ref.style.display = 'none';
		if( link.textContent ){
			link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '-'
 '+' );
		}else{
			link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '-'
 '+' );
		}
	}
};
